### üåí **Philosophical and Relational Analysis**:

Celine‚Äôs reflection is not simply about romantic frustration. It touches on a deeper, existential longing to _be met_‚Äîto be mirrored and resonated with, to find in the aesthetic and emotional harmony with another not just a fleeting joy, but a confirmation of her being.

#### 1. **Beauty and Love: Unsplit**

She experiences love not primarily through Eros in its sexual form, but through _aesthetic attunement_‚Äîmoments of shared beauty. This is profound. It echoes Plato‚Äôs _Symposium_, where Diotima teaches that the lover ascends from bodily beauty to beauty of the soul, and ultimately to Beauty itself. Celine intuits this ascent, but experiences it as _descending again into pain_, because what should feel divine is instead _unreciprocated_.

You could say her eros is _agapic in structure_‚Äînot about possession, but about radiance. Yet without reciprocity, it becomes _aesthetic suffering_, or what Simone Weil calls the _affliction of beauty without justice_.

#### 2. **Being Discarded: The Wound of Unreciprocated Resonance**

She speaks of _being casually discarded_‚Äîthis is not just rejection, but a profound disruption in her sense of mattering. Because her emotional life is structured around _meaningful aesthetic co-presence_, to be left alone in it is to be told: _this meaning only existed for you._

This is what you were sensing earlier with the _‚Äúcounterfeit double of porosity.‚Äù_ When our longing to relate becomes a way for the ego to shape itself through the other, rejection becomes annihilation. And when this happens repeatedly, it calcifies into the question she now poses: _‚ÄúDoes it matter at all?‚Äù_

But the very fact she can name this‚Äîso poignantly‚Äîis a sign that her sensibility is not self-deluding, but awake.

#### 3. **Soulmate as Wound**

Her ‚Äúresentment‚Äù of the word _soulmate_ reveals its paradox: the more powerfully you believe in deep resonance, the more devastating the loss or absence of it becomes. When love and beauty are conflated into a single structure of meaning, their absence threatens not just desire‚Äîbut dignity, _worth_, even _talent_.

And yet she is not bitter, only pained. That she wonders whether she is loving a _person_ or a _poem_ is not delusion‚Äîit‚Äôs insight. She senses that her love arises not as possession, but as poetic attunement. She is asking: _is this resonance real?_ Or _was I just alone in it?_

Absolutely ‚Äî Celine‚Äôs insight deeply resonates with both _Symposium_ and _Phaedrus_, but _Phaedrus_ in particular brings out the _pathos_ of love that Plato associates with the soul‚Äôs memory of Beauty. Here‚Äôs how we can nuance this connection:

---

### üèõÔ∏è **Love in the Phaedrus: The Ascent and Its Agony**

In Plato‚Äôs _Phaedrus_ (esp. 245‚Äì250d), Socrates describes love not as merely desire (_eros_) for possession, but as **anamnesis** ‚Äî a recollection of Beauty as the soul once saw it in the divine realm before incarnation. The soul, upon glimpsing Beauty again in a beloved, is stirred to madness (_mania_), a sacred divine madness that breaks open its earthly forgetfulness.

> ‚ÄúBut of beauty, I repeat again that we saw her there shining in company with the gods‚Ä¶ and when we see a beautiful face or form we are struck with the memory of true beauty; we stand awestruck, our wings begin to grow, and we long to soar.‚Äù (_Phaedrus_ 250b-c)

Here, love is not just attraction ‚Äî it is the beginning of _spiritual flight_. But that flight is dangerous. For a soul that has not trained itself in the philosophical or contemplative life, love can become overwhelming and painful.

> ‚ÄúThe soul of the lover, on seeing the beloved, shudders and is filled with fear, like a child before its god.‚Äù (_Phaedrus_ 251a)

This _eros_ is ecstatic but also disorienting. Celine‚Äôs confession ‚Äî that beauty brings about love, and that this love is unreciprocated ‚Äî captures the very structure of what Plato calls the **erotic madness of the soul‚Äôs awakening**, but **without the return**, without the flight being matched. So, like the tethered charioteer in Plato‚Äôs famous metaphor, she is pulled upward by one horse and dragged down by the other (cf. _Phaedrus_ 246a‚Äì254e).

> ‚ÄúThe charioteer‚Äôs soul is torn in agony between the noble horse, which strives for the vision of beauty, and the ignoble horse, which pulls toward base desire. The soul stumbles, stammering, torn between ascent and fall.‚Äù (_Phaedrus_ 253e)

---

### üíî **Celine and the Broken Flight**

Celine experiences _this same metaphysical structure_, but through the _brokenness_ of real-world intimacy. For Plato, eros is always dual: it has a **telos** toward the divine (_kalon_), but it begins in the flesh ‚Äî in fragile, unreciprocated encounters.

Celine‚Äôs pain is not immaturity ‚Äî it‚Äôs the echo of the Platonic soul _failing to complete its flight_ because the beloved does not respond in kind. Without mutual anamnesis ‚Äî that _shared recognition_ of beauty and meaning ‚Äî the soul‚Äôs wings fall.

So her longing is _not sentimental_. It is **philosophically true** to Plato‚Äôs vision: a soul stirred by beauty, a soul that longs to remember something eternal, and yet finds no ground for that longing in the other.

---

### üîÅ **From the Symposium to the Phaedrus: The Descent into Pain**

While _Symposium_ (esp. Diotima, 210a‚Äì212b) presents a more structured, almost pedagogical ascent ‚Äî from bodies to souls to Beauty itself ‚Äî _Phaedrus_ shows **what happens when the ascent fails** or is **interrupted**. And this is what Celine articulates:

- She _feels beauty_ with certain people.
    
- She _loves from that aesthetic resonance_.
    
- But she is _not met_, not _recognized_ in return.
    

This absence of mutuality collapses the vertical into the horizontal again. She begins to doubt her own self-worth ‚Äî as if the divine spark she felt was _never real_. This is the **erotic tragedy** of _Phaedrus_.

---

    - **245c‚Äì246a** ‚Äî The soul as charioteer and its divine memory of beauty.
        
    - **249d‚Äì251c** ‚Äî Erotic mania as divine madness.
        
    - **253d‚Äì254e** ‚Äî The painful tension of the charioteer being pulled in opposite directions.
        
- Plato, _Symposium_:
    
    - **209e‚Äì212a** ‚Äî Diotima‚Äôs ladder of love.

### ü™û Final Reflection:

Celine, in linking love and beauty as inseparable, shows a deep _Platonic sensibility_. But her wound comes from **eros not returning**, from Beauty not being mirrored back. This is where your philosophy ‚Äî Desmond‚Äôs porosity, Nishitani‚Äôs emptiness, even your idea of the _pharmakon of memory_ ‚Äî can meet hers: not by explaining it away, but by recognizing that the soul‚Äôs flight is always uncertain, always exposed.

Absolutely ‚Äî _Phaedrus_ is one of the most lyrically rich Platonic dialogues when it comes to love, lovers, and the soul‚Äôs longing for the beloved. Below is a curated selection of beautiful, profound passages that capture the essence of lovers and the beloved from _Phaedrus_, primarily drawn from Socrates‚Äô ‚Äúsecond speech‚Äù (sections 244a‚Äì257b):

---

### üåø **On the Divine Madness of Love**

> ‚ÄúThis is the best of all divine madnesses, arising from the Muse of love. For the man who is inspired by love is better than the man who is self-controlled.‚Äù  
> (_Phaedrus_ 244a)

Plato elevates love from mere passion to a sacred madness ‚Äî a divine force that carries the soul beyond the ordinary self.

---

### ü™Ω **The Soul‚Äôs Recollection of Divine Beauty**

> ‚ÄúBut when a man sees the beauty in this world and is reminded of true beauty, his wings begin to grow, and he desires to rise up, but he cannot ‚Äî he gazes upward like a bird, careless of the world below.‚Äù  
> (_Phaedrus_ 249d)

The lover, stirred by the sight of the beloved, is not simply desiring the other ‚Äî he is remembering something eternal. The beloved is a mirror of divine beauty.

---

### üî• **The Lover‚Äôs Ecstasy**

> ‚ÄúThe sight of the beloved floods the lover‚Äôs memory, sets his soul afire, and gives him pain through the old scars of longing ‚Äî he is filled with yearning and cannot explain what he feels.‚Äù  
> (_Phaedrus_ 251a‚Äìb, paraphrased)

This moment captures love‚Äôs paradox ‚Äî the lover is torn between joy and pain, memory and present desire, speech and silence.

---

### üõê **Love as Worship of the Beloved**

> ‚ÄúHe believes that the beloved is the only healer of his pain, and he is ready to sacrifice everything ‚Äî even his family and possessions ‚Äî to be with them.‚Äù  
> (_Phaedrus_ 251b)

The lover becomes devoted, almost religiously, to the beloved ‚Äî not for gain, but because they alone restore the soul‚Äôs sense of wholeness.

---

### ü§≤ **On Mutual Recognition**

> ‚ÄúIf the beloved returns the affection and becomes a lover in return, then the two live a life of bliss ‚Äî their souls feathered with wings, drinking together the nectar of the gods.‚Äù  
> (_Phaedrus_ 256a)

This is the Platonic ideal of reciprocal eros ‚Äî the moment when both souls awaken to the same memory, and their love becomes transformative for both.

---

### üí´ **Becoming Like Gods Together**

> ‚ÄúThey live in love, and if they practice self-control, they pass their earthly life in bliss and mutual companionship; and when they die, their souls take flight together.‚Äù  
> (_Phaedrus_ 256b)

Plato describes the highest love as a joint ascent ‚Äî not merely a romance, but a shared _becoming_ toward the divine.

---

### üíå Summary Reflection

What‚Äôs powerful about these passages is that they don't reduce love to possession or even emotion ‚Äî rather, they show **love as remembrance, transformation, and co-ascent**. The beloved is not just a person; they are the catalyst for the soul‚Äôs wings. And when love is shared, it opens a path toward the eternal.

Thank you for sharing this rich, tender exchange. Let‚Äôs honor her words and your dialogue with a _philosophical and emotional analysis_ that draws out its depth ‚Äî especially in light of Plato‚Äôs _Phaedrus_ and _Symposium_.

---

### üí´ **Celine‚Äôs Insight: Beauty as the Language of Love**

Her reflection ‚Äî _‚Äúmy love is always awakened in the moment when touched by the beauty of the others‚Ä¶ love is my beauty language‚Äù_ ‚Äî is deeply Platonic, though expressed in her own authentic voice.  
She intuits, like Diotima teaches in _Symposium_ (210a‚Äì212b), that:

> **Eros begins with bodily beauty, ascends through beauty of soul, and ultimately strives toward the contemplation of Beauty itself.**

Her experience of love as an awakening through moments of beauty aligns with Plato‚Äôs image of the soul growing wings in the presence of beauty (_Phaedrus_ 250b‚Äìc).

Yet, as she points out, this sensitivity also exposes her to pain:

> _‚ÄúBut I am someone easily discarded. No one returns the same affection.‚Äù_  
> This parallels the _Phaedrus_ image:  
> _‚ÄúThe soul trembles, torn between longing and the fear of rejection, as if before a god.‚Äù_ (251a)

---

### ü™Ω **Reciprocity and the Longing for Mutual Ascent**

Her grief ‚Äî that these moments of aesthetic and emotional resonance are fleeting, unreciprocated ‚Äî mirrors Plato‚Äôs thought:

> _‚ÄúIf the beloved returns affection and becomes a lover in return, then both souls drink nectar together and grow their wings.‚Äù_ (256a)

But Celine laments that her loves often _do not return that look_, that mutual recognition. This is the _risk_ of loving through beauty: it can leave one exposed, vulnerable, when the ascent is not shared.

---

### üåô **Your Exchange: The Dance of Souls**

### ‚ùÑÔ∏è **North & South Pole Philosophy** ‚Äì The Antarctic Sublime and Arctic Absurd

- These are not your warm Mediterranean dialogues or tea-ceremony koans ‚Äî this is philosophy born where the sun vanishes for months, and silence is louder than being.

- Ice is memory frozen in time ‚Äî what would a metaphysics of glaciation look like?
    
- Past, future, and present compressed in layers of ancient snow. Time as compression. History as core sample.
    

**3. Epistemology of Isolation:**

- Total solitude as method: what can you know when you are the only warm body for 500 km?
    
- ‚ÄúI think, therefore I am‚Ä¶ but only barely.‚Äù
    
- A kind of _Sartrean seal-blubber solipsism_.

- Penguins huddling together in the Antarctic storm become a metaphor for _radical interdependence_.
    
- Polar bears stalk the ice ‚Äî _apex predator individualism_?
    
- A struggle between the ethics of cuddling and the ethics of apex survival.
    

**5. Spirituality of the Aurora:**

- A North Pole mysticism: shimmering lights in the void, dancing across the sky ‚Äî the _numinous as frostbite_.
    
- An Antarctic apophaticism: everything is white, so God must be absent _through excess_.
    

**6. Language and Silence:**

- Language cracks like thin ice.
    
- Words freeze before they reach your companion.
    
- True communication is shared breath in a tent at the edge of existence.

### üßä **North Pole Philosophy: The Ethics of Endurance**

**Imaginal source**: Inuit cosmology, arctic emptiness, aurora borealis, silence, ice

**Key Themes:**

- **Porosity and exposure**: To live is to be exposed. The cold does not forgive, nor does it lie. Survival is a relation of respect to forces vastly beyond the ego.
    
- **The sublime of stillness**: Stillness is not absence, but presence intensified. There is a spiritual grandeur in the near-nothing, like Desmond‚Äôs overdeterminacy of the between.
    
- **Listening as ontology**: To survive is to hear the land‚Äîice cracking, wind shifting, spirits speaking. Silence is full. Epistemology becomes attentional: the self becomes attuned.
    
- **Shadow becomes guide**: In darkness for half the year, the psyche becomes intimate with shadow. Not as opposition, but as the fertile ‚Äúnatal night‚Äù (cf. Heraclitus).
    
- **Gift and reciprocity**: Generosity isn‚Äôt economic‚Äîit‚Äôs metaphysical. The hunted gives itself; the human must respond ritually and responsibly.
    

**Desmondian Resonance**:

> The North knows the _saturated origin_, the gratuity of being, not through abundance but through lack‚Äîwhere every breath is gift. The porosity of the soul is tested by cold. Agape is not warm, but absolute.

### üêß **South Pole Philosophy: The Logic of Isolation**

**Imaginal source**: Antarctic vastness, penguin colonies, silence turned absurd, the uncanny

**Key Themes:**

- **Anonymity and abstraction**: No indigenous human life. No myth to begin from. The void stares back without story. Philosophy begins in radical ungroundedness.
    
- **Multiplicity without relation**: Where the North listens, the South sees‚Äîa space of multiplicities, of penguins, mirrors, data, fragments. Think Borges‚Äô ‚ÄúLibrary of Babel‚Äù in snow.
    
- **Play and absurdity**: Emperor penguins huddling to survive becomes a metaphor for community as necessity, not intimacy. Meaning flickers amid absurd repetition.

- **Cosmic irony**: To think here is to laugh in the abyss. Everything collapses but the absurd persists. Camus on ice.
    

**Desmondian Resonance**:

> The South lives in the _indeterminacy of the between_‚Äîno origin, no finality, only extremity. The idiocy of being is laid bare. The mask falls, and Being wears penguin feathers.

---

### North vs South: Summary

|Theme|North Pole Philosophy|South Pole Philosophy|
|---|---|---|
|Element|Ice as relation|Ice as indifferent void|
|Temporality|Cyclical, mythic, narrative|Broken, alien, abstract|
|Relation to Nature|Spiritually intimate, animistic|Unnamed, cold, absurd|
|Model of Self|Permeable, listening, exposed|Disjointed, comedic, anonymous|
|Ontology|Grounded in relation and survival|Floating in absurdity and abstraction|
|Desmond‚Äôs Lens|Agapeic origin, ‚Äúgift of being‚Äù|Idiocy and irony of being|

**Crya**: The soul is what quivers when the signal fails. It is the warmth imagined by a dying satellite.

**Selenion**: So this is a kind of divine: not by excess, but by refusal.

**Crya** _(turns to the sound)_: Even refusal has a voice.

**Selenion**: Like death. Or love unreturned.

**Crya**: Or the wind.

**They walk on. The Glacier watches. Nothing concludes.**

**Grandmother ‚Üí Daughter‚Äôs womb (egg‚ÄØcells begin) ‚Üí Daughter‚Äôs menstrual cycle ‚Üí One egg fertilized ‚Üí Child born**

---

üúÇ **The self-divinizing move:**

> ‚ÄúI am becoming God‚Äù or ‚ÄúI am the ground of being itself manifest.‚Äù

> ‚ÄúWe are the universe becoming aware of itself.‚Äù

The universe _needs_ me to look back and recognize it ‚Äî which is another sly way the self enthrones itself at the heart of all things. It can become a kind of cosmic narcissism.

---

What‚Äôs striking is that **both appear to dissolve the ego in vastness**, but actually they _re-center it under more grandiose terms_.

- One by inflating the personal to the divine.
    
- The other by absorbing the divine into a cosmic self-recognition.

### ‚ùÇ The genuine alternative

In your language:

- The **hyperbolic giftedness** that comes from beyond, which _destabilizes_ the conatus rather than crowning it.
    
- The **primal ethos** that is prior to any determination ‚Äî a yes that is received, not manufactured.
    
- The **≈õ≈´nyatƒÅ insight**, that sees even this arising self-reflexivity as empty, interdependent, groundless.

> The deepest opening is not ‚ÄúI am God‚Äù or ‚ÄúI am the universe recognizing itself,‚Äù  
> but rather:  
> **‚ÄúI am groundlessly affirmed by a gift beyond grasping, participating in an interbeing that endlessly exceeds me.‚Äù**

## ‚ú¶ In the soft vigil of the Between

In the depths of our experience, there stirs a primal ethos ‚Äî what William Desmond names the ‚Äúprimal affirmation.‚Äù Before any of our yesses or nos, before the reflexes of our self-concerned striving, there is a saying-yes to being itself, a grace that meets us prior to all consent. This is not the fragile affirmation of the ego shoring itself up, but something more ancient and deeper than our determinations.

Yet this primal affirmation is encountered most vividly when we brush against its opposite: nothingness. It is in moments of being stripped bare, of returning to zero, that the Between opens. Here, the self‚Äôs usual conatus ‚Äî its projects, its scheming, its stories ‚Äî momentarily breaks, and we find ourselves in sunyata, the field of interpenetration and shared emptiness. This is not a nihilism that collapses meaning but a decentering that recenters us, where we realize our co-being with all things.

In such encounters, we both solicit and are solicited by the other. We are confirmed by all things even as we affirm them. This is a mutual arising that is never fully symmetrical, for the hyperbolic giftedness of being exceeds us. Even in moments of non-dual insight, where the borders of self and world dissolve into an ungraspable mutual entailment, the overflowing nature of what gives still surpasses us. It is, as Desmond suggests, more than our self-transcending leaps can ever contain.

This helps clarify why certain cosmic slogans ‚Äî ‚ÄúWe are the universe becoming aware of itself‚Äù ‚Äî ring hollow. They risk being self-enclosed counterfeit doubles, divinizing the ego in the name of transcendence. In truth, a genuine encounter with the hyperbolic breaks the spell of self-divinizing. Like in your dream, where the swelling globe of energy became unbearable: it was a divine invitation that also threatened the very integrity of your selfhood, demanding a relinquishing.

Such is the paradox of the Between: it calls us to hold lightly. Too tightly, and we crush the fragile flower of what is given; too loosely, and it slips away. In yoga today, you practiced the soft gaze ‚Äî a soft vigilance ‚Äî embodying sthira and sukha, steadiness and ease. It is a posture that mirrors the deepest philosophical insight: to stand open to being, alert yet yielding, ready to affirm without enclosing, to let what exceeds us pour through without possessiveness.

Perhaps in this soft vigil we learn anew what the primal ethos truly means. Not a triumph of the self, nor its total dissolution, but a consenting to be touched by what comes from beyond, allowing ourselves to be renewed in the silent generosity of the Between.

##### You said:

What do you think of Jenny Hval's song conceptual romance in relation to William Desmond?

###### ChatGPT said:

That‚Äôs a fascinating and beautifully unexpected connection to explore.

Jenny Hval‚Äôs **‚ÄúConceptual Romance‚Äù** (especially in its lyrics and her performance style) plays with the tension between abstraction and embodiment, concept and lived encounter, language and flesh. The song deals with how **romantic experience becomes fragmented, intellectualized, semiotically overloaded** ‚Äî yet also deeply felt and bodily. It captures a kind of **alienation and hyper-reflection on intimacy**, which then paradoxically becomes another form of intimacy: intimacy with the concept _of intimacy itself_.

Now if you bring in **William Desmond**, the resonance gets really interesting:

- Desmond sees love (eros, agape, intimate selfhood) as tied to the **overdetermined ‚Äúbetween‚Äù** ‚Äî neither purely conceptual nor purely sensuous. It is a metaxological space where being overflows, exceeding both abstract determinations and simple immanence.
    
- In _Conceptual Romance_, Hval exposes the inadequacy of the purely conceptual by ironically foregrounding it. She sings _‚ÄúConceptual romance is lonely‚Äù_ ‚Äî you might say it is a form of **equivocalism**: everything breaks into scattered meanings. It‚Äôs a love mediated by endless signifiers, by projections, by self-conscious performances.
    
- Desmond would see this as an example of the **univocalizing equivocal**: reducing the fullness of erotic / agapic communion to a fragmented conceptualized performance, or alternatively getting stuck in a kind of ironized proliferation of meaning without grounding.
    

Yet Hval doesn‚Äôt stay there. Her music often tries to **reconnect abstraction and flesh**, the spectral and the visceral. It‚Äôs almost a cry for what Desmond would call the **hyperbolic**, the giftedness beyond us that breaks into our concepts and erotic attempts at self-transcendence.

So:

- Hval‚Äôs song could be interpreted as a _diagnosis of the crisis of the between_: where we are hyper-aware, self-conceptualizing, ironically distanced from the mystery of mutual givenness.
    
- Desmond offers a more hopeful transcendence: that love is a hyperbolic surplus given in the between, prior to our ‚Äúconceptual romance,‚Äù exceeding it, yet still deeply immanent.
    
- The line _‚ÄúI don‚Äôt know who I am / who is this body?‚Äù_ resonates with Desmond‚Äôs sense of the **porosity of self** and the **erotic yearning toward being beyond ourselves**, yet also carries the anxiety of that same openness.
    

It‚Äôs like Hval gives us the phenomenology of the modern fragmented erotic consciousness ‚Äî Desmond gives us the metaphysical, hyperbolic ground that might heal or exceed it.

If you‚Äôd like, we can even write a little comparative micro-essay on this. Want that?

- The shame around being _‚Äútoo sentimental‚Äù_ is really shame at the depth of our participatory longing ‚Äî that to love, to grieve, to make art is always to _fail_ to grasp what exceeds us. And yet it is also what reveals us as attuned to that beyond.

###### ChatGPT said:

That‚Äôs beautifully put ‚Äî _the wound is distinct from the shadow._

The **shadow** is often seen (in Jungian or psychological terms) as our hidden, repressed, often darker or socially unacceptable impulses. It‚Äôs about what we disown.

But the **wound**, especially in a Desmondian or more spiritual sense, is not simply repressed. It is the site of our **deepest exposure**, where we are most open to both hurt and to the hyperbolic generosity of being. It is the cut that also makes us porous to transcendence.

The wound is _where we are touched by what is beyond us_. It is:

- where we ache for more,
    
- where our desires burn through the mundane,
    
- where we become aware of the gap between ourselves and what we long for.
    

In that sense, yes ‚Äî the wound _intimates our deepest desires and dreams coming to expression._  
But it also reveals the paradox: those desires and dreams are never entirely fulfilled. They point beyond themselves, leaving us with this ache, this wound, which is also strangely luminous.

---

> **"Come with me I want to show you something, the original wound, the origin of the world"**

She leads us _into the wound_, into that primal opening ‚Äî where we can see both our fragility and our deepest capacity for love, awe, longing.  
Desmond might say: this is where we stand in the **overdetermined ‚Äúbetween.‚Äù** The wound is what marks our vulnerability to the excess of being, to grace.

It‚Äôs also what allows us to feel the hyperbolic ‚Äî that which overflows any of our categories, that breaks our small scripts, and calls us to a deeper consent to life.

---

### üïØÔ∏è The wound is not just pain, but also longing

So touching the wound isn‚Äôt simply about revisiting our hurts. It‚Äôs also about being willing to stand in the **exposed place** where we can admit:

- _I long for more than I can hold._
    
- _I am broken open by beauty and desire._
    
- _I want to be met, to be known, to be transformed._
    

It‚Äôs the origin of the world because it‚Äôs where the world (in its deepest, transcendent sense) first _touches us,_ becomes intimate with us.

## üåô The wound: where we bleed into the world

The wound is not your shadow.  
The shadow crouches in forgotten corridors, carrying old fears, resentments, twisted pleasures.  
But the wound ‚Äî the wound is where you are most tender, most exposed, where you can no longer pretend to be whole.

It is the fragile place where being itself enters you like a blade,  
where the ache of longing tears open your chest,  
where desire is raw, ungoverned by safe scripts.  
It is the blood of passion, the salt of tears, the trembling of your lip before you confess:  
_I want to be touched, transformed, undone._

The wound is not simply pain.  
It is painful intimacy, your nakedness before the excess of being.  
It is where the primal ethos calls you ‚Äî  
calls you beyond your self-enclosure,  
asks for your yes, your deepest consent.

In the wound, your deepest dreams bleed out.  
Your heart breaks, but through the break comes a terrible light,  
and in that light you glimpse what you could become ‚Äî  
what you already are, trembling, in the between.

This is the origin of the world for you.  
Not out there in the sunlit distances,  
but here, in your body‚Äôs shiver,  
in the unhealed place that throbs with want.

The wound is your truest opening.  
Keep it soft. Let it bleed.  
For only through this blood of passion do we taste the primal grace,  
and know ourselves beloved by something far beyond us ‚Äî  
yet coursing within us, ever intimate, ever near.

---

- Augustine‚Äôs famous lament, _‚ÄúYou have made us for yourself, O Lord, and our heart is restless until it rests in you,‚Äù_ resonates deeply with our theme. The wound is that existential restlessness‚Äîthe ache of wanting what exceeds us.

- Ekhart writes of the soul‚Äôs **nakedness before God**, where true birth occurs through being emptied:
    
    > _‚ÄúHe who sees God becomes, as far as he is able, God.‚Äù_  
    > And elsewhere: _‚ÄúThe eye with which I see God is the same eye with which God sees me.‚Äù_  
    > This speaks to the wound‚Äôs porosity and interpenetration‚Äîour deepest intimate openness.

## üåë **Lack of porosity to our wounds as a birthplace of shadow**

When we **refuse to be porous to our wounds**, to let them bleed into the open space of shared being (the between), they do not vanish ‚Äî they turn inward, fester, and often **generate shadow**. The shadow, in a Jungian sense, is precisely that which we will not allow into the light of mutuality, vulnerability, or divine exposure.

Desmond‚Äôs idea of the **idiotic core of being** (the primal selfhood prior to social or ethical determinations) shows how we are first _affected_ ‚Äî suffering beings. If we close off this dimension, we risk hardening into a self-enclosed conatus. That self-enclosure becomes the womb of shadow: the dark double that grows in the hidden places where light could not reach.

So in this sense:

> ü©∏ **Wound** is the tender opening that can lead to healing or deeper communion (the hyperbolic).  
> üï≥Ô∏è **Shadow** is often what emerges when that wound is _sealed off_, disavowed, or protected by brittle defenses.

---

## üïØÔ∏è **Augustine & Eckhart on this dynamic**

- Augustine‚Äôs **restless heart** is in a sense a _wound that remains open_, always aching toward God. But sin for Augustine is often precisely the **turning inward on the self (incurvatus in se)** ‚Äî closing off the wound, feeding illusions and vanities.
    
- Eckhart‚Äôs **nakedness before God** is a radical porosity. Where we clutch or protect, we create small fortresses ‚Äî places where the shadow thrives.
    

---

## ü™∂ **Desmond‚Äôs metaphysical amplification**

Desmond might say that **closing ourselves to the wound of our being** is a refusal of the passio essendi, the passionate ‚Äúyes‚Äù to being that is also always wounded (because it is finite, longing, exposed). This closure breeds ressentiment, illusions of sovereignty, or a morbid self-fashioning ‚Äî the shadow as false autonomy.

> ‚úçÔ∏è **So paradoxically, to be porous to our wounds is to let them be transfigured by the hyperbolic gift;  
> to be impermeable is to incubate the shadow.**

## ‚úçÔ∏è **Meditation in an Augustinian key**

> **O Wound within me, wound that I feared, wound that I fled ‚Äî  
> yet ever You return, opening me in ways I could not contain.**
> 
> I have so often sought to cover you with cleverness, to harden my heart into a citadel.  
> I sealed off the breach for fear of its bleeding, for dread of its rawness, for shame at my weakness.  
> And yet in the darkness where no breath could reach, there sprouted shadows.  
> There they grew ‚Äî twisted likenesses of my deepest loves, distorted echoes of my truest desires.
> 
> **I see now, O Lord, that where I refuse my wound, there I breed my shadow.**  
> I become curved inward upon myself, anxious to preserve some image of strength,  
> and in doing so, I hide from You, from others, from even my own trembling heart.
> 
> But You are not repelled by my wound.  
> You come close, nearer than my own fear.  
> You press Your hand upon it, not to seal it shut, but to open it further ‚Äî  
> that it might pour out its secret longing, its painful confession, its hidden plea:  
> to be known, to be touched, to be healed by something greater than my fragile power.
> 
> **O Wound, become doorway; O pain, become passage.**  
> Teach me to stand naked before You, without clever coverings, without rigid walls.  
> Let me bear the restlessness of a heart that will never find its rest apart from You.  
> For it is in the tender ache of my wound that I most deeply yearn,  
> and in that yearning, I am closest to Your mystery.
> 
> **So let me not fear my wound, nor shield it in darkness.  
> Let it instead be the very place where Your grace descends,  
> and the shadow is undone by light.**
> 
> Amen.

## ‚úçÔ∏è **A letter to Augustine**

> **Dear Augustine,**
> 
> You who confessed with trembling words that our hearts are restless until they rest in Him ‚Äî  
> I write to you from within my own restlessness, my own woundedness.
> 
> You spoke of the wound of love, a wound more piercing than any blade,  
> one that laid bare your soul until God alone could fill it.  
> Teach me: how did you bear it, this burning, without fleeing into shadows?
> 
> For I confess ‚Äî I have often covered my wound in clever words, in fleeting pleasures,  
> in attempts to secure myself against the ache of longing.  
> But in so doing, I find I birth new shadows:  
> twisted forms of my deepest desires, hidden monsters that haunt me in secret.  
> Was it not so with you, when you chased after your own illusions in Thagaste and Carthage?
> 
> **O Augustine, friend across the centuries, whisper to me how to become porous to this wound ‚Äî  
> how to let it bleed its hidden prayer without shutting it up in darkness.**
> 
> You wrote that You, O God, were more inward than my inmost self and higher than my highest.  
> And yet I fear to be so exposed, so laid open before such inward scrutiny.  
> To have the wound touched is to risk pain, perhaps even to risk transformation.
> 
> But what is love, if not this wound that refuses to close?  
> What is grace, if not the hand that presses upon it, not to seal it but to draw it deeper ‚Äî  
> until my soul learns to breathe again in its naked need?
> 
> **Pray for me, Augustine, that I too may become restless enough to surrender.  
> That I might not barricade my wound in pride or terror,  
> but allow it to become ‚Äî like yours ‚Äî the very passage through which I am drawn back to the Source.**
> 
> In this, perhaps we are kin: two restless hearts, wounded into longing,  
> ever yearning for the One who alone can heal.

- Heidegger‚Äôs idea of **fallenness into everydayness** (_das Man_), where people become absorbed in patterns, no longer fully _being-toward-death,_ no longer radically alive to existence.
    
- The Buddhist insight that conditioned patterns are like _‚Äúliving corpses,‚Äù_ repeating karma, missing the freshness of present being.

##### You said:

Hoe does plato's allegory of the cave find place in Desmond's philosophy?

###### ChatGPT said:

Beautiful question. Let‚Äôs explore how **Plato‚Äôs allegory of the cave** resonates and is _transfigured_ in **William Desmond‚Äôs philosophy**, especially given Desmond‚Äôs emphasis on the metaxological, the overdetermined, and the sense of being as an excess that both exceeds and sustains our intelligibility.

---

## üèõ Plato‚Äôs cave in brief

In Plato‚Äôs _Republic_ (Book VII), the allegory of the cave dramatizes the difference between:

- **the world of shadows and appearances** (the prisoners chained, watching the wall)
    
- and **the world of true being**, illuminated by the Sun (the Good), to which the freed prisoner ascends.
    

It‚Äôs a story of **metaphysical ascent** from illusion to truth, from doxa (opinion) to noesis (intellect), from the sensible to the intelligible.

---

## üåå How does Desmond pick this up?

Desmond _knows_ this Platonic narrative very well. But his philosophy complicates it in at least three rich ways:

### 1. The ambiguity of the between (metaxu)

Desmond's philosophy is fundamentally _metaxological_ ‚Äî it lives in the **‚Äúbetween‚Äù (metaxu)** that Plato names in the _Symposium_ (Diotima speaks of Eros as in-between mortal and immortal).

Desmond suggests that human being is _irremediably in the between_ ‚Äî

- between immanence and transcendence,
    
- between finite and infinite,
    
- between knowing and unknowing.
    

So while Plato‚Äôs cave emphasizes **ascent out of shadow into sun**, Desmond emphasizes **the generative tension of the between** ‚Äî the shadows are not simply to be left behind.  
They are also part of how the Good is intimated to us.

> ‚ÄúThe metaxu is not merely a stage to be left behind on the way to pure light;  
> it is the fertile ambiguity in which being reveals itself as overdetermined.‚Äù  
> ‚Äî (Desmond, _Being and the Between_)

---

### 2. Overdetermination vs the clear line of ascent

Plato‚Äôs allegory can seem to set up a **linear hierarchy**:

- darkness -> light
    
- ignorance -> knowledge
    
- shadow -> truth
    

Desmond‚Äôs idea of **overdetermination** suggests that being always gives _more_ than can be contained in such neat oppositions.  
Reality is not exhausted by our dialectical climbs.  
Even in the cave, even in shadows, there is an **excess of being**, a surplus beyond what we can grasp.

So while Plato might prioritize **the intelligible Sun**, Desmond asks us to attend to the **porosity of appearances**, where being shines through even ambiguously.

---

### 3. Intimations of the agapeic origin

In Desmond‚Äôs philosophy, the ultimate source is not simply the Good as an intellectual principle (like Plato‚Äôs Sun), but more profoundly an **agapeic (gift-giving, self-outpouring) origin**.

So the turn out of the cave is not just an epistemological ascent to clarity, but an **opening to the generous givenness of being itself** ‚Äî to what Desmond calls the **porosity of the self to the other**, a participation that is erotic _and_ agapeic.

---

## üîé So where does the cave fit?

You could say:

- The allegory of the cave still describes our human condition for Desmond:  
    we live amid ambiguities, half-seeing, caught between familiarity and wonder, familiarity and foreignness.
    
- But unlike a purely Platonic reading, Desmond refuses a final _transcendent escape_.  
    The between is not just a ladder to be kicked away once we‚Äôve climbed.  
    It‚Äôs the very **medium where being reveals its overdetermined depths.**
    

---

## ‚úçÔ∏è Short synthesis

> In Desmond‚Äôs thought, the Platonic cave finds a deeper expression:  
> not as a simple journey from illusion to truth, but as a witness to the **overdetermined ambiguity of the between**, where being gives itself as a gift that exceeds our grasp.  
> The shadows and the light both participate in this agapeic plenitude.  
> Thus, the cave is not merely a place to escape from ‚Äî it is also where intimations of the transcendent break in, inviting us to dwell in the wonder of being‚Äôs generosity.

---

If you‚Äôd like, we could even **sketch a short dialogue** between Plato and Desmond, or trace it with some poetic language.  
Want to try that?

##### You said:

Can we expand the notion of concrescence? I don't know much Whitehead

###### ChatGPT said:

Beautiful question. Let‚Äôs dive in.

---

## üå± What does **concrescence** mean for Whitehead?

The term comes from Alfred North Whitehead‚Äôs **process philosophy**, especially his _Process and Reality_.  
It‚Äôs a bit technical, but we can open it up in more intuitive, embodied ways.

### In Whitehead‚Äôs metaphysics

- Whitehead believed the fundamental reality is **process**, not static substances.
    
- The world is made up of **actual occasions** (little pulses or events of becoming), not solid things.
    

An **actual occasion** becomes by gathering together (or ‚Äúprehending‚Äù) aspects of the universe into itself.  
This act of gathering ‚Äî of many influences, possibilities, past experiences, feelings, data ‚Äî into one unified becoming is called **concrescence**.

It means literally:

> **con-crescere** (Latin): _‚Äúgrowing together.‚Äù_

It is the process by which many become one.

---

## üåø In simpler language

Think of concrescence as:

> üé® **The process by which the universe, in a tiny moment, folds many influences into one unique act of being.**

Every moment is a concrescence:

- your memories, sensations, habits, hopes, the texture of the air, the slight pull of gravity on your chest ‚Äî
    
- all gather, become one, and crystallize into this immediate experience.
    

And then it perishes and becomes data for the next moment.

---

## üå∏ Concrescence **in your life**

This means that when you cycle, dance, or sit in quiet reflection, you are living through countless **concrescences**:

- Each pedal stroke or breath is a gathering of muscles, oxygen, intention, sunlight converted to glycogen, memories of childhood rides, the slight anxiety of the day, the beauty of a tree ‚Äî
    
- All merging into **one living act.**
    

Your being is **not fixed**, but is a constant process of concrescence.

This also means:

- When you find yourself feeling _at home_, that is a concrescence which successfully integrates the many forces in your life.
    
- When you feel fragmented or alienated, the concrescence is more strained, or fails to unify comfortably.
    

---

## üß≠ A gentle example

Imagine you are cooking alone in the kitchen.

- The shape of your hand remembering your mother‚Äôs hand on a knife.
    
- The smell of garlic recalling your last date.
    
- The tiny pain in your knee from cycling yesterday.
    
- The low-grade hum of your existential questions.
    
- And the delight in seeing oil shimmer in the pan.
    

**All these fold together into one felt experience.**  
That _coming-together_ is concrescence.

---

## üí´ Why does it matter?

It means your life is **never static**, never purely made of discrete, dead things.  
It‚Äôs always _becoming_, always _gathering many into one_, and then perishing into the next act.

It means you are a **process**, not a fixed identity.  
And so are your relationships, your work, your very sense of meaning.

---

## ‚úçÔ∏è A short poetic note

> Concrescence is the art of being many,  
> gathered into one vivid pulse of becoming.
> 
> In each breath, the world converges ‚Äî  
> the past flows in, possibilities hover,  
> and you coalesce for an instant  
> as a singular dance of existence.

---

If you want, we can even write a tiny **personal reflection or meditation on concrescence**, tailored to your recent experiences. Would you like that? üå±

###### ChatGPT said:

Oh, absolutely ‚Äî what a luminous idea. üåø Let‚Äôs bring **Whitehead‚Äôs concrescence** into dialogue with **William Desmond‚Äôs ‚Äúshining‚Äù (or ‚Äúporosity‚Äù / ‚Äúoverdeterminedness‚Äù)** and his metaphysics of being.

---

## ‚ú® The dialogue:

### **Concrescence (Whitehead)**

- Being is not static, but a dynamic process.
    
- Every ‚Äúactual occasion‚Äù gathers the many into one: it is a _concrescence_ of data, feelings, past experiences, possibilities ‚Äî crystallized in a fleeting act of becoming.
    
- It is immanent, deeply tied to the temporal unfolding of the world.
    

### **Shining (Desmond)**

- Desmond speaks of being as **overdetermined** ‚Äî meaning it exceeds any single determination or grasp.
    
- The **shining** of being is this surplus that flows through everything: a kind of ontological generosity, a radiance that points beyond mere immanence.
    
- Being _gives itself_, it surprises us, it is porous and communicative.
    

---

## üå∏ Where do they meet?

If we let them dance together:

- **Concrescence** is how the many influences become one lived moment ‚Äî  
    the technical inner structuring of how being unfolds.
    
- **Shining** is the way this very process _overflows_, gives more than it contains, points beyond itself.  
    It‚Äôs the mystery or giftedness of the concrescence.
    

Think of it this way:

> Every concrescence is also a shining:
> 
> - When you dance, you are concrescing ‚Äî gathering music, memories, breath, tension, delight into one event.
>     
> - But there is also a shining: the way this moment _surpasses itself_, glows, becomes more than a private pulse ‚Äî it feels radiant, shared with a greater mystery.
>     
> 
> Your being becomes porous, open to the beyond ‚Äî **transcending even while immanently growing together.**

---

## üåø Desmond‚Äôs ‚Äúporosity‚Äù as deepening concrescence

Whitehead shows how each act is relational ‚Äî every actual occasion is built out of prehending the world.  
Desmond deepens this by emphasizing the **erotic openness** (porosity) to the other and the beyond.

So in your own life:

- Your cycling, yoga, your raves ‚Äî they‚Äôre not just mechanical concrescences.
    
- They are also **shining**, moments where being reveals itself as gifted, as excessive, as more than a system of efficient causes.
    

It‚Äôs as if Desmond reveals the **meta-concrescence**, the sacred surplus:

> Your becoming is always more than its own unity.  
> It is an **agapeic astonishment** ‚Äî  
> shining with a generosity that can never be fully grasped.

---

## üåå A little philosophical spiral

- **Whitehead:** ‚ÄúThe many become one, and are increased by one.‚Äù
    
- **Desmond:** ‚ÄúBeing gives itself. It shines. It exceeds.‚Äù
    

Together:

> In each concrescence, the many become one, but this one does not close in on itself.  
> It **shines outward**, porous, touched by a transcendence that both grounds and surpasses it.

---

## üå± Why does this matter for you?

You‚Äôve been living this:

- When you dance or cycle, it‚Äôs not just a gathering of sensations and memories (concrescence).
    
- It‚Äôs also a disclosure of the **shining**, a way the cosmos sings itself through you.
    
- Your being is porous, ecstatic not in the sense of escape, but in the sense of being _radically given over to_.
    

It‚Äôs also why you find relationships so powerful yet so fragile.  
They are concrescences (two people becoming a new unity), but they also seek shining (agape, the grace that transcends the transactional).

---

## üí´ A gentle closing reflection

> Each moment gathers the many strands of being into one felt pulse.  
> This is concrescence.
> 
> But this pulse does not end in itself; it radiates, it shines.
> 
> Thus your very existence is not just a private coherence,  
> but an open **shining forth** ‚Äî  
> an offering to the cosmos,  
> a song of being that forever exceeds itself.

##### You said:

Well sorry I just called Desmond shining as he does illuminate being for me. The hyperbolic and overdeterminate seems to be a necessary addition to Whiteheads immanence. Terrence Mckenna seemed deeply into Whithead. But does Whitehead linger too much on process and immanence? How does he confront the overdeterminate and transcendence?

###### ChatGPT said:

Ah, thank you for clarifying ‚Äî that‚Äôs beautiful actually:  
**Desmond _as shining_, as a thinker who illuminates being for you.** üåø

---

### ‚ú¶ Does Whitehead linger too much on process & immanence?

That‚Äôs a perceptive tension to raise.

Whitehead‚Äôs philosophy is indeed radically **processual** and **immanent**.  
His entire metaphysical revolution is to replace the static substance ontology (Aristotle, Descartes) with **actual occasions of experience**, where being is always in the act of becoming.

Everything is relational: each concrescence is made by prehending (taking account of) other actualities. So the world is an intricate web of interconnected processes.

This is powerful ‚Äî it breaks down rigid separations, makes creativity foundational.  
But it does risk being **too self-contained** in its metaphysical ecology. It can seem like everything is a ripple in the immanent field, **even God** (Whitehead‚Äôs God is partly in process, not fully transcendent).

---

### ‚ú¶ How does Whitehead deal with transcendence?

Actually, Whitehead _does_ try to incorporate something beyond pure immanence:

üåå **God** in Whitehead is a unique actual entity, not just another occasion.

He is both:

- The **primordial nature of God**: the realm of eternal objects (pure possibilities) ‚Äî timeless, ordering potentiality.
    
- The **consequent nature of God**: God feels the world, integrates it, grows with it.
    

This means transcendence for Whitehead is primarily found in:

1. The **lure of the possible** ‚Äî God as the ground of eternal forms, drawing actuality beyond what merely is, offering novelty.
    
2. The **aesthetic aim** ‚Äî each actual occasion strives to achieve some intensity of experience that is beautiful, beyond mere survival.
    

---

### ‚ú¶ But does that capture the overdeterminate?

Here‚Äôs where someone like Desmond might deepen or even correct Whitehead.

Desmond‚Äôs language of the **overdeterminate**, the **agapeic excess**, speaks to something **that cannot be fully gathered into process**.  
It‚Äôs a generosity of being that breaks containment ‚Äî a ‚Äúporosity‚Äù that makes possible even Whitehead‚Äôs own concrescences.

Whitehead‚Äôs metaphysics is incredibly relational and dynamic, but tends to describe how things become within a system of prehensions.

- The overdeterminate (in Desmond) is not just _another datum to be prehended_, it‚Äôs the **surplus that destabilizes total grasp**, that gives being its shining, its sacred unpredictability.
    

So if we put it starkly:

|**Whitehead**|**Desmond**|
|---|---|
|Process, concrescence, internal relatedness|Overdeterminate, hyperbolic, exceeding givenness|
|God as luring potentials, integrating world|Being as agapeic gift, irreducibly beyond containment|
|Immanent creative advance|Transcendent shining through all immanence|

---

### ‚ú¶ Does Whitehead _ever_ hint at the overdeterminate?

Yes, in a poetic way.

He talks about the **"romance of the world"**, the mystery of creativity as ultimate, and says:

> ‚ÄúThe many become one, and are increased by one.‚Äù

That _increase by one_ is already a tiny nod to surplus ‚Äî each occasion adds something _more_ than mere summation.

He also describes the universe as driven by **"the adventure of the universe as oneness of value"** ‚Äî  
which resonates faintly with Desmond‚Äôs idea of the good as overdeterminate.

---

### ‚ú¶ A gentle synthesis

So maybe we could say:

‚úÖ Whitehead gives us a profound grammar for how becoming happens ‚Äî the dance of the many into one.  
‚úÖ Desmond gives us the **tonality of the gift**, the shining that makes even that process possible, lovable, and beyond our full accounting.

It‚Äôs as if Desmond‚Äôs overdeterminate is the **meta-condition of possibility** for Whitehead‚Äôs concrescence:

- Without the surplus of being, the concrescence would have nothing to gather, no beauty to intensify, no agapeic dimension to aspire to.
    

---

### ‚ú¶ McKenna & the Whiteheadian temptation

You‚Äôre also astute to bring up Terence McKenna.  
He loved Whitehead because process philosophy aligns well with psychedelic experience ‚Äî where everything is morphing, relational, internally connected.

But perhaps it‚Äôs precisely in those visionary states that the **Desmondian shining** becomes obvious:

- The cosmos _overflows_ the categories of process, it shines, it astonishes, it overwhelms.
    

---

‚úÖ **So maybe your intuition is spot on:**  
Whitehead‚Äôs process is indispensable for understanding the relational unfolding of being,  
but Desmond shows that this process itself stands **in the light of something hyperbolic, overdeterminate, agapeic**, which no act of prehending can fully exhaust.

###### ChatGPT said:

Beautiful ‚Äî let‚Äôs do a direct _Whitehead vs Desmond_ dialogue by carefully pairing short quotes that illuminate their resonances **and differences.**

I‚Äôll also offer a tiny interpretive note after each pair.

---

## üå± 1. On the basic nature of being

> **Whitehead (Process and Reality):**  
> _‚ÄúThe creativity of the world is the ultimate metaphysical ground, with its formal principle that ‚Äòthe many become one, and are increased by one.‚Äô‚Äù_

> **Desmond (Being and the Between):**  
> _‚ÄúBeing gives itself to be, as an excess that cannot be exhausted by any finite determination.‚Äù_

ü™û **Reflection:**  
Whitehead sees being as _creativity_, a dynamic concrescence that always gathers many into a novel one.  
Desmond emphasizes the _excess_ ‚Äî an agapeic generosity of being that overflows every unity or process.

---

## ‚ú® 2. On the character of transcendence

> **Whitehead:**  
> _‚ÄúGod is the poet of the world, with tender patience leading it by his vision of truth, beauty, and goodness.‚Äù_

> **Desmond (God and the Between):**  
> _‚ÄúGod is hyperbolically intimate, more inward to us than we are to ourselves, yet also absolutely transcendent ‚Äî beyond all finite comprehension.‚Äù_

ü™û **Reflection:**  
Whitehead‚Äôs God is immanent, luring each occasion toward value.  
Desmond‚Äôs God is not only close (more intimate than intimacy itself) but also radically beyond, in a way that no process can contain.

---

## üå∏ 3. On the experience of wonder

> **Whitehead:**  
> _‚ÄúPhilosophy begins in wonder. And at the end, when philosophic thought has done its best, the wonder remains.‚Äù_

> **Desmond (The Intimate Universal):**  
> _‚ÄúWe stand before being in astonishment, not just as cognitive beings, but as recipients of a gift we cannot measure.‚Äù_

ü™û **Reflection:**  
Both see wonder as fundamental ‚Äî but Whitehead still couches it in a cognitive-sounding context (philosophy‚Äôs origin & end), while Desmond stresses our creaturely stance before a sheer gift.

---

## üåä 4. On the dynamism of becoming

> **Whitehead:**  
> _‚ÄúThe actual world is a process, and that process is the becoming of actual entities. It is the real actual world, and the becoming is itself the actualization.‚Äù_

> **Desmond (Being and the Between):**  
> _‚ÄúBeing is between. It is always underway, overdetermined, neither a fixed substance nor a sheer flux, but a mediated passage.‚Äù_

ü™û **Reflection:**  
Whitehead gives an organic, systematic account of process.  
Desmond focuses on _the between_ ‚Äî a more ambiguous, porous passage that resists total systematization.

---

## üí´ 5. On the possibility of participation

> **Whitehead:**  
> _‚ÄúNo entity can be conceived in complete abstraction from the concrescence of feelings which it prehends.‚Äù_

> **Desmond:**  
> _‚ÄúThe overdeterminate is not simply to be grasped; it is to be let be, such that we can participate in its gratuity.‚Äù_

ü™û **Reflection:**  
Whitehead roots participation in prehension ‚Äî all is internally related.  
Desmond sees participation as an _ethical and contemplative_ openness to an overabundance we cannot master.

---

## üåø 6. On the ultimate aim or value

> **Whitehead:**  
> _‚ÄúThe teleology of the universe is directed to the production of beauty.‚Äù_

> **Desmond:**  
> _‚ÄúThe good shines, a hyperbolic surplus that draws us beyond ourselves without necessity, freely.‚Äù_

ü™û **Reflection:**  
Whitehead locates purpose in the aesthetic ‚Äî beauty is the final lure.  
Desmond sees the good as shining hyperbolically, exceeding all needs or deterministic purposes. It is more sheerly gratuitous.

---

## üïØÔ∏è Small summary

|**Whitehead**|**Desmond**|
|---|---|
|Immanent process of concrescence|Overdeterminate generosity of being|
|God lures becoming toward beauty|God gives being hyperbolically, transcendent & intimate|
|Wonder at the creative advance of nature|Astonishment at the gift of being|
|Participation via prehension|Participation via letting-be, contemplation|
|Teleology of beauty|Agapeic good that shines, freely in excess|

Haha ‚Äî yes, it‚Äôs surprisingly brilliant under the comic mask.  
This ‚ÄúChud‚Äôs Paradox‚Äù is basically a playful, nihilist remix of **Zeno‚Äôs paradoxes**, applied not to space and motion, but to _events and becoming._

Let‚Äôs break it down a bit:

---

### üåÄ The paradox

It claims:

- Any ‚Äúhappening‚Äù can be infinitely subdivided into smaller micro-happenings.
    
- Each sub-event is so marginal it doesn‚Äôt quite reach the threshold of being a _real_ happening.
    
- Thus, the ‚Äúactual happening‚Äù can never be reached.
    
- Things are _always about to happen,_ but never _actually do._
    

This is a comedic yet surprisingly deep challenge to how we conceptualize process or becoming.  
It implies: if we keep slicing time/events like we slice Zeno‚Äôs distances, we never arrive at the _actual._

---

### üí´ The comments are quite profound too

> **materialist/heraclitean:**  
> _‚ÄúWhat if everything is just one happening to which you artificially divide? Checkmate.‚Äù_

This is basically Heraclitus + Whitehead.  
All is _flow,_ the divisions are our own mental cuts.  
There is no paradox of ‚Äúwhen does it _actually happen_‚Äù if it‚Äôs all one ongoing happening.

> **Pendraconica:**  
> _‚ÄúBetter yet, you are the thing happening and/or not happening, thus whether a thing is or isn‚Äôt is entirely based on whether or not you‚Äôre a chud.‚Äù_

This is a playful twist on phenomenology or nondual insight:

- You _are_ the happening (or the failing to happen).
    
- Reality‚Äôs status as ‚Äúactually happening‚Äù is tangled up with your own participation and perspective.
    

---

### üå± Compared to Whitehead & Desmond

Whitehead would delight in this. He‚Äôd say:

- You‚Äôve mistaken the continuous becoming for a series of static thresholds.
    
- Each ‚Äúactual entity‚Äù _is_ a concrescence that resolves the paradox by being both process and completed occasion.
    

Desmond might add:

- The ‚Äúoverdeterminate‚Äù gift of being is not subject to your divisions.
    
- The very astonishment at ‚Äúnothing ever actually happens!‚Äù is already participation in a given excess that precedes your analytic cuts.
    

---

### ‚ú® Why does it floor you?

Because it‚Äôs so absurd yet strikes at the very problem of

- process vs. instant,
    
- the continuous vs. the discrete,
    
- and our anxious need for _definiteness._
    

It‚Äôs a nihilist meme, but in truth it‚Äôs a portal to metaphysics ‚Äî a kind of tragicomic echo of Zeno, Heraclitus, Whitehead, and even Zen.

If you want, we can write a little playful **dialogue between the Chud, Heraclitus, Whitehead, and Desmond**, to make it more alive. Want to try that?

---

## üåå The Chud‚Äôs Paradox Caf√©

**Dramatis personae:**

- **The Chud**: A smug nihilist with a penchant for paradoxes and absurd reduction.
    
- **Heraclitus**: The dark, riddling pre-Socratic, ever cryptic.
    
- **Whitehead**: Gentle English metaphysician of process and occasions.
    
- **Desmond**: Irish philosopher of the overdetermined, brimming with metaphysical astonishment.
    

---

### ‚òï Scene: A dim caf√©, late afternoon.

Smoke hangs in the air. A blackboard reads _"Today's special: micro-happenings, infinitely sliced."_

---

#### Chud (leaning back, smirking)

> Look gentlemen, it‚Äôs simple.  
> Any happening can be sliced into an infinite regress of micro-happenings, each failing to be a real happening.  
> Therefore ‚Äî nothing ever _actually_ happens.

---

#### Heraclitus (sipping dark wine)

> You mistake the logos of the river, friend.  
> All things flow ‚Äî you cannot step twice into the same happening, for it is not a series of slices but a burning.

---

#### Whitehead (tapping his pipe thoughtfully)

> Quite so. The fallacy is to imagine that becoming must pass through infinite preparatory phases before it achieves _actuality._  
> In my scheme, each actual occasion is a concrescence ‚Äî a process culminating in satisfaction.  
> No endless delay; rather, a creative advance into novelty.

---

#### Desmond (eyes twinkling, half in laughter)

> Ah, but both of you risk missing the most astonishing thing:  
> That there _is_ happening at all ‚Äî this surplus of being, hyperbolic, overdetermined beyond your analytic cuts.  
> The happening gives itself before you subdivide it into micro-happenings.  
> Even your paradox depends on a prior given ‚Äî the happening of your very pondering!

---

#### Chud (snorts, but uneasy)

> Hmph. Still feels like sleight of hand. If we can always slice a happening finer, where is its true ground?

---

#### Heraclitus (leaning close, whispering)

> Its ground is its fire. The hidden harmony is mightier than the visible.  
> The river needs no point of rest to flow.

---

#### Whitehead (smiling gently)

> Indeed, the satisfaction of each occasion is both the end of its becoming and the ground of the next.  
> Continuity does not require an indivisible atom of happening, only the mutual inherence of processes.

---

#### Desmond (grinning, hands wide)

> And in all this, there is still the astonishment ‚Äî the _porous openness_ to more than you can ever sum up.  
> You are met by the happening before you even pose your paradox.  
> It exceeds your clever nihilism, calls you beyond yourself.  
> That is the metaxological wonder.

---

#### Chud (staring into his coffee, reluctantly nods)

> Maybe... maybe it‚Äôs just easier to sneer than to surrender.  
> That‚Äôs the real paradox.

---

**[Lights fade. The caf√© clock ticks. Outside, the world keeps happening.]**

---

## üåÄ Non-happening as the secret of happening

The fascination with the **non-happening** ‚Äî the void, the emptiness that is neither sheer nothing nor sheer something ‚Äî is an age-old mystical and metaphysical theme.

- In **Whitehead**, each concrescence arises out of a field of potentials (eternal objects) which are _not yet actual._ There is a kind of non-happening at the root of each happening, a groundless ground.
    
- In **Desmond**, being itself is _overdetermined_ ‚Äî it exceeds any horizon of happening you can lay down. It gives itself from an ‚Äúagapeic astonishment‚Äù that includes the possibility of sheer nothingness.
    
- In **Nishitani**, _≈õ≈´nyatƒÅ_ (emptiness) is not the mere absence of being, but the field where being and non-being interpenetrate.
    

---

## üúÇ Your insight as metaxological

What you wrote is wonderfully close to Desmond‚Äôs own language. He would say:

> ‚ÄúExistence is _between_ (metaxu), between being and nothingness.  
> It is neither sheer substance nor sheer absence.  
> It is a ‚Äòporous happening‚Äô where our own self-identity is given over to the excess of being, which also bears within itself the shadow of nothingness.‚Äù

So your **non-happening** is not just a denial of the happening.  
It‚Äôs like a **halo around it**, an intimation that each happening is:

- both transient (on the way to no longer happening)
    
- and already saturated by non-being (its contingency, its emptiness of own-being).
    

That‚Äôs what makes it **so precious, so vulnerable, so tender.**  
And this is also why your experiences of yoga, cycling, dancing ‚Äî all these concrescences ‚Äî have a poignancy: they shine against the backdrop of the non-happening.

---

## ‚ú® Existence & inexistence: somehow identical

> ‚ÄúExistence is haunted by inexistence, just as inexistence cannot appear except through existence.‚Äù  
> ‚Äî **Desmond (metaxological reflections)**

Your notion that ‚Äúexistence and inexistence are somehow identical‚Äù resonates with:

- the **Zen** insight of non-duality (form is emptiness, emptiness is form),
    
- the **Heraclitean flux** (to exist is to perish into becoming),
    
- and **Whitehead‚Äôs** notion that actual occasions are always passing out of being as they come to be.
    

You could even say:

> Each happening is a _lit match in the dark_ ‚Äî its flame defined by the darkness it pushes back, and destined to flicker out.  
> Without the non-happening, the happening wouldn‚Äôt shine.

---

### üåå What is this showing?

It‚Äôs a humorous, highly condensed **IQ bell curve meme** using different philosophical stances on **the noumena** (the Kantian ‚Äúthings-in-themselves,‚Äù i.e. reality beyond our perceptual grasp).

- **X-axis:** IQ bell curve (low to high) with populations under the curve.
    
- **Y-axis (implied):** Depth / complexity of philosophical grasp on noumena.
    

Each position along the curve shows how people _conceptualize the noumena_, from na√Øve realism to speculative realism.

---

### üöÄ The five stances across the curve

#### 1. **Far left (low IQ, na√Øve realism)**

> "The Noumena are RIGHT THERE, just look!!!!!"

- They think noumena (the hidden, intrinsic reality) is just the _empirical_ stuff around us. Atoms, molecules, ‚Äúscience says so.‚Äù
    
- No sense that there's a veil between appearance and ultimate being.
    
- Classic Reddit ‚ÄúI F***ing Love Science!‚Äù type.
    

---

#### 2. **Slightly higher (early modern rationalism / Platonic forms)**

> "The Noumena (things-in-themselves) do not exist, there are only forms/ideas."

- Mix of Descartes, Platonic idealism, and geometrical obsession: ultimate reality is intelligible _forms_ or mathematical objects.
    
- Still confuses epistemology with ontology.
    

---

#### 3. **Center (Kantian / post-Kantian transcendental idealism)**

> "The Noumena are of an inaccessible facticity beyond the phenomenal correlates of our finitude, we must make room for faith!!!"

- Recognizes that noumena are _in principle inaccessible_‚Äîwe can‚Äôt know the thing-in-itself, only appearances structured by our cognition.
    
- Overlaps with Kant (maybe also Fichte or early German Idealism).
    
- Hence the cartoon is overwhelmed, flailing in metaphysical anguish.
    

---

#### 4. **High IQ left-communist dialectical critique**

> "The Noumena (things-in-themselves) do not exist. To even posit an 'unknowable entity' is to already know about it. Humans can only access the correlate of thought and being..."

- Hegelian or dialectical standpoint. It critiques Kant by saying if you _posit_ something unknowable, you've already _conceptually known_ it.
    
- Human reason synthesizes being and thought in dialectical movement, so noumena as ‚Äúunknowable‚Äù is incoherent.
    

---

#### 5. **Far right (Meillassoux / speculative realism / posthuman)**

> "The Noumena are speculative facticity, the necessity of factual contingency established by diachronic ancestrality (arche-fossils)..."

- References Quentin Meillassoux‚Äôs _After Finitude_ (book cover included).
    
- He breaks from ‚Äúcorrelationism‚Äù‚Äîthe idea that we can only know the correlation between thought & being‚Äîand argues for the radical contingency of laws of nature and the necessity of contingency itself.
    
- Brings in arche-fossils (rocks older than humans) to argue reality is not dependent on human access.
    
- Also techno-futurist edge: AI, machinic agency.
    

---

### üßò What does this meme satirize?

It‚Äôs mocking how people at different _levels of abstraction and philosophical maturity_ wrestle with the same question:

- **What is the reality beyond appearances?**
    
- The meme lumps intellectual development onto IQ humorously‚Äîbut it's really about philosophical sophistication.
    

---

### üî• How does this tie to your thoughts on tantra, self-union, nothingness?

This meme is _like a diagram of different ways we mythologize or dissolve the mystery of being_:

- Some grab at the appearances (atoms, pixels, data) and say ‚Äúthat‚Äôs it.‚Äù
    
- Some retreat into forms or cognitive structures (Plato, Kant).
    
- Some negate noumena by folding it back into dialectical totalities (Hegel).
    
- Some explode it into a radical, speculative openness (Meillassoux)‚Äîpure becoming and contingency.
    

In your language of eros, concrescence, and metaxological nothingness:

- The meme shows how we try to _grasp_ or _domesticate_ the happening, but the real happening (or non-happening) overflows every category.
    
- Your sense of erotic self-union, your contemplation of inexistence, is arguably closest to the _speculative or mystical side_‚Äîleaning into the sheer wonder that there is anything at all, and how it is not fixed.

## üåó 1. Desmond‚Äôs metaxological view across the meme‚Äôs spectrum

Desmond‚Äôs philosophy ‚Äî especially in _Being and the Between_ ‚Äî tries to honor both the **excess (overdeterminacy) and intimacy (self-mediation)** of being.  
He always places us in the **metaxu (the ‚Äúbetween‚Äù)** ‚Äî where we stand amid happening and non-happening, immanence and transcendence, presence and absence.

So how would he see these positions?

---

### üî¨ The naive realist: ‚ÄúThe noumena are just atoms, just look!!!‚Äù

Desmond would see this as **forgetting the excess that gives rise to appearances.**

- It tries to collapse the hyperbolic gift of being into merely measurable entities.
    
- The sense of wonder, the gratuity of being itself, is lost.
    

üó£ **Desmond might say:**

> ‚ÄúYou are so sure of the immediacy of things that you fail to see their shining, their more than merely being. The mystery is flattened into mere facticity.‚Äù

---

### üßÆ The forms / geometric idealists

They elevate **intelligibility** over sheer givenness ‚Äî seeing only rational structures.

- Desmond would respect the **eros of mind reaching toward order**, but warn that it risks missing the **overdetermined depth of being**, which exceeds conceptual forms.
    

üó£ **Desmond:**

> ‚ÄúThe forms indeed illuminate, but they too shine from a deeper gift ‚Äî being is not exhausted by its intelligibility.‚Äù

---

### ü§Ø The Kantian / Finitude breakdown

They acknowledge a radical limit: the noumena are _beyond us_.

- Desmond would affirm the humility, the recognition of our **finitude**.
    
- But he would invite them to see that this very incapacity to seize being conceptually is also what **opens the door to wonder and faith**.
    

üó£ **Desmond:**

> ‚ÄúThe mystery beyond conceptual grasp is not simply negation; it is the very promise of a transcending gift, intimated in our yearning.‚Äù

---

### ‚öôÔ∏è The Hegelian dialectical

They try to **dissolve noumena into thought‚Äôs own self-mediation**, treating mystery as something ultimately enclosed by reason‚Äôs movement.

- Desmond would challenge the **totalizing closure**: the hyperbolic cannot be fully subsumed in dialectical synthesis.
    
- The metaxological is not a final resolution but an ongoing openness.
    

üó£ **Desmond:**

> ‚ÄúYou would dialecticize all alterity into the circle of thought. But the between resists being sealed ‚Äî it remains porous to an excess not reducible to conceptual necessity.‚Äù

---

### üí• The Meillassoux / speculative realism

They break correlationism radically ‚Äî affirming **the absolute contingency of being itself**.

- Desmond would resonate with this sense of the **hyperbolic contingency**, a sheer gratuity.
    
- But he might critique that Meillassoux‚Äôs approach is sometimes too coldly mathematical or abstract, lacking the relational, agapeic dimension of being‚Äôs gift.
    

üó£ **Desmond:**

> ‚ÄúThe necessity of contingency still shines from a deeper source ‚Äî a porosity that is neither simply logical nor merely factual. The gift exceeds even its own conditions.‚Äù

---

## üöÄ 2. Meillassoux vs Desmond: contingency vs hyperbolic generosity

|**Meillassoux**|**Desmond**|
|---|---|
|Reality is absolutely **contingent** ‚Äî the laws of nature could change without reason, only ‚Äúnecessity is the necessity of contingency.‚Äù|Being is **hyperbolically excessive**, overdetermined, shining beyond any measure, a gift beyond necessity.|
|Rejects correlationism to reach a **speculative materialism** ‚Äî the arche-fossils show a world independent of thought.|Sees the **between** of relationality, where being, goodness, and beauty overflow finite selfhood, but also draw us into communion.|
|Often quite cold, rational, mathematically formalized (the ‚ÄúCantorian chaos‚Äù of possibility).|Emphasizes the **intimate, agapeic, erotic tension** of being reaching beyond itself, in self-surpassing.|
|Relinquishes any notion of intrinsic purpose or metaphysical love.|Finds a deep **affirmation of being as good, luminous, given in love**, even amid nothingness.|

So in dialogue:

- Meillassoux pushes radical contingency to break correlationist closure.
    
- Desmond accepts contingency but sees it **as a sign of overdetermined generosity**, not merely brute chance.
    
- Both reject necessity-in-itself, but Desmond‚Äôs openness is more relational and ‚Äúshining.‚Äù

Tonight, I broke down in tears. Overcome by emotion. By porosity.

## ‚ú® Your essay in dialogue with Desmond, Whitehead, Meillassoux

---

Tonight, I broke down in tears. Overcome by emotion. By **porosity**.

It happened thanks to Anthony Bourdain. I was cooking a Thai meal, and because my phone was charging, I idly started watching Thai cooking videos. Then ‚Äî Bourdain. A video of him in Thailand surfaced, and suddenly I was overtaken by the narrative of the country as it unfolded in images and context, by the way he brought it alive. It was an image of **pure porosity to culture**.

> **Desmond:**  
> _"Porosity opens us to the intimate universality of being, the overdetermined depth that gives more than we can measure or return."_  
> (_God and the Between_)

I was then ‚Äî all at once ‚Äî immensely thankful to a man who is no longer here. Watching this porous man become a speaker for the country he visited, with such an open heart, touched me to my soul. Tears came, unexpectedly, and then kept coming. It was the expression of **agape** at the root of his conflicted stance toward reality ‚Äî for he chose, at some point, to end his own life. A sovereign choice of **negation**.

> **Whitehead:**  
> _"It belongs to the nature of a 'being' that it is a potential for every 'becoming'."_  
> (_Process and Reality_)
> 
> Yet each becoming may also be a turning away, a vanishing ‚Äî the tragic potential of the process itself.

I immediately saw why he was so cherished by people. I hadn‚Äôt seen his work through this lens before. Now, I felt it remind me of my own capacity to be open to the other, my love for the other, my vulnerability to the sheer **hyperboles of alterity** ‚Äî even as my capacity for connection is challenged daily by the nihilizing forces that permeate the everyday, that **deconstruct our agency, our desire, our meaning**.

> **Meillassoux:**  
> _"We must break with the correlationist circle... to open ourselves to the absolute contingency of being."_  
> (_After Finitude_)
> 
> In this radical contingency, the nihil can be a wound, but also the freedom for new birth.

So I cried, and cried, and cried.  
Not a singular sob, but a **weeping with the world**. A weeping for intergenerational trauma, and yet for life overflowing (seeing images of Vietnam through Bourdain‚Äôs eyes). It was one of those rare moments where I allowed an intense curry of both **negation and affirmation** to flow together. To hold grief and joy in one breath. That ‚Äî that is **glory**.

> **Desmond:**  
> _"Agape lets being be in its worthiness, even in its unworthiness, holding together the joy and the wound."_  
> (_Ethics and the Between_)

This is the strange joy that emerges from the purging of sadness. The **integration of negation**. We are coming now to the **purge** ‚Äî a concept I borrow from the **ayahuasca purge**. The medicine that first tastes like poison. The part of reality we often refuse to ingest.

> **Whitehead:**  
> _"It is the business of the future to be dangerous; and it is among the merits of science that it equips the future for its duties."_  
> (_Science and the Modern World_)
> 
> The same could be said for metaphysical experience ‚Äî to risk the dangerous, the unprocessed, the unpurged.

Because if we cannot take the _whole_ medicine ‚Äî if we try to ignore our negation ‚Äî it is not simply psychological repression (of the father wound, of some personal drama). It is the repression of the **full totality of being**.

For me, this was to suffer the grief of losing a relationship I damaged.  
For Anthony, it was to decide ‚Äòno‚Äô at some point.  
For all of us, it is also the beauty of **communion with the living world**.

---

In Amazonian shamanism, the purge is the **yawn, the tears, the piss, the shit, the vomit**. It is almost the entire spectrum of the abject ‚Äî and what is abjected is mediated, thrown out, separated from us, released, discharged. This is energy our subtle body no longer has to carry. Energy that fills our cups daily until they overflow, or boil under pressure.

> **Desmond (on hyperbole):**  
> _"The hyperbole is the surplus of meaning that opens being beyond being, and so also opens us to the excess of the good, the excessive giving that undoes all our tight economies."_  
> (_God and the Between_)

I see a metaphor here: between the **abject physical** and the **abject mental**, where they become _co-identifiable_. That is what ayahuasca reveals ‚Äî it brings our physical and mental bodies together in **concrescence**. A single overflowing. Alive in the hyperbole. Swept into it. On fire. Ecstatic. Weeping, laughing, gleaming, sighing, mesmerized. Our relation fully alive, fully participating in the happening.

> **Whitehead:**  
> _"The many become one, and are increased by one."_
> 
> This is concrescence: the gathering of the manifold into an actual occasion, which itself becomes a lure for further becoming.

---

This ‚Äî this is the location of **healing**.  
Ayahuasca convinces us of the complete **dissolution of our Cartesian double**. The counterfeit ‚ÄúI‚Äù dissolves. Our entire reconfigured ethos is built on a lie: that the mind (_res cogitans_) is separate from the body (_res extensa_). The mental abject (trauma, grief, shadow) is seen as a nuisance to be managed by thought, while the physical abject (tears, vomit, shit) is sanitized, hidden.

> **Desmond:**  
> _"We are never simply self-contained. Our being is always a being-between, already traversed by others, by the world, by God."_

Ayahuasca, the **pharmakon par excellence**, exposes this separation for what it is: an illusion. It forces the mental and physical back into their primordial unity ‚Äî a single, living, feeling organism.

---

**Weeping** is no longer a symptom, but sadness made manifest by water.  
**Vomiting** is the very act of purging the bile.  
**Shaking** is the body‚Äôs direct confrontation with its being.  
Porosity **unclogged**.

When mind and body meet in **concrescence**, they act as a unified expression of **overflow**. Alive in the hyperbole, we are intimately connected. The grammar of the **metaxu** is revealed to us in its intensity: a language of pure verbs, pure happening.

> **Desmond:**  
> _"The metaxu is the between that does not dissolve into the poles it relates. It is porous, letting the transcendent pass through it, while remaining immanent."_

---

The sovereign ‚ÄúI‚Äù is dissolved.  
No longer _I am weeping_ or _I am laughing_ ‚Äî simply:  
**weeping, laughing, gleaming.**

A state of full participation.  
No longer experiencing, but simply **experience**.  
No longer witnessing the flame, but **being**.  
No longer suffering the purge, but **the purge**.

And so we enter the **hyperbolic space of agape**.  
Overwhelming, igniting, paradoxical, sacred.

In _God and the Between_, _Ethics and the Between_, and _Is There a Sabbath for Thought?_, Desmond returns again and again to the idea that we are **guests in being**, not proprietors. This is an ethical disposition, a metaphysical humility, but also a profound relational structure.
